    18	//! The GlobalOrderRequire optimizer rule either:
    19	//! - Adds an auxiliary `OutputRequirementExec` operator to keep track of global
    20	//!   ordering and distribution requirement across rules, or
    21	//! - Removes the auxiliary `OutputRequirementExec` operator from the physical plan.
    22	//!   Since the `OutputRequirementExec` operator is only a helper operator, it
    23	//!   shouldn't occur in the final plan (i.e. the executed plan).
    24	
    25	use std::sync::Arc;
    26	
    27	use crate::PhysicalOptimizerRule;
    28	
    29	use datafusion_common::config::ConfigOptions;
    30	use datafusion_common::tree_node::{Transformed, TransformedResult, TreeNode};
    31	use datafusion_common::{Result, Statistics};
    32	use datafusion_execution::TaskContext;
    33	use datafusion_physical_expr::Distribution;
    34	use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::OrderingRequirements;
    35	use datafusion_physical_plan::projection::{
    36	    make_with_child, update_expr, update_ordering_requirement, ProjectionExec,
    37	};
    38	use datafusion_physical_plan::sorts::sort::SortExec;
    39	use datafusion_physical_plan::sorts::sort_preserving_merge::SortPreservingMergeExec;
    40	use datafusion_physical_plan::{
    41	    DisplayAs, DisplayFormatType, ExecutionPlan, ExecutionPlanProperties, PlanProperties,
    42	    SendableRecordBatchStream,
    43	};
    44	
    45	/// This rule either adds or removes [`OutputRequirements`]s to/from the physical
    46	/// plan according to its `mode` attribute, which is set by the constructors
    47	/// `new_add_mode` and `new_remove_mode`. With this rule, we can keep track of
    48	/// the global requirements (ordering and distribution) across rules.
    49	///
    50	/// The primary use case of this node and rule is to specify and preserve the desired output
    51	/// ordering and distribution the entire plan. When sending to a single client, a single partition may
    52	/// be desirable, but when sending to a multi-partitioned writer, keeping multiple partitions may be
    53	/// better.
    54	#[derive(Debug)]
    55	pub struct OutputRequirements {
    56	    mode: RuleMode,
    57	}
    58	
    59	impl OutputRequirements {
    60	    /// Create a new rule which works in `Add` mode; i.e. it simply adds a
    61	    /// top-level [`OutputRequirementExec`] into the physical plan to keep track
    62	    /// of global ordering and distribution requirements if there are any.
    63	    /// Note that this rule should run at the beginning.
    64	    pub fn new_add_mode() -> Self {
    65	        Self {
    66	            mode: RuleMode::Add,
    67	        }
    68	    }
    69	
    70	    /// Create a new rule which works in `Remove` mode; i.e. it simply removes
    71	    /// the top-level [`OutputRequirementExec`] from the physical plan if there is
    72	    /// any. We do this because a `OutputRequirementExec` is an ancillary,
    73	    /// non-executable operator whose sole purpose is to track global
    74	    /// requirements during optimization. Therefore, a
    75	    /// `OutputRequirementExec` should not appear in the final plan.
    76	    pub fn new_remove_mode() -> Self {
    77	        Self {
    78	            mode: RuleMode::Remove,
    79	        }
    80	    }
    81	}
    82	
    83	#[derive(Debug, Ord, PartialOrd, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]
    84	enum RuleMode {
    85	    Add,
    86	    Remove,
    87	}
    88	
    89	/// An ancillary, non-executable operator whose sole purpose is to track global
    90	/// requirements during optimization. It imposes
    91	/// - the ordering requirement in its `order_requirement` attribute.
    92	/// - the distribution requirement in its `dist_requirement` attribute.
    93	///
    94	/// See [`OutputRequirements`] for more details
    95	#[derive(Debug)]
    96	pub struct OutputRequirementExec {
    97	    input: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
    98	    order_requirement: Option<OrderingRequirements>,
    99	    dist_requirement: Distribution,
   100	    cache: PlanProperties,
   101	}
   102	
   103	impl OutputRequirementExec {
   104	    pub fn new(
   105	        input: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   106	        requirements: Option<OrderingRequirements>,
   107	        dist_requirement: Distribution,
   108	    ) -> Self {
   109	        let cache = Self::compute_properties(&input);
   110	        Self {
   111	            input,
   112	            order_requirement: requirements,
   113	            dist_requirement,
   114	            cache,
   115	        }
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    pub fn input(&self) -> Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan> {
   119	        Arc::clone(&self.input)
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    /// This function creates the cache object that stores the plan properties such as schema, equivalence properties, ordering, partitioning, etc.
   123	    fn compute_properties(input: &Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>) -> PlanProperties {
   124	        PlanProperties::new(
   125	            input.equivalence_properties().clone(), // Equivalence Properties
   126	            input.output_partitioning().clone(),    // Output Partitioning
   127	            input.pipeline_behavior(),              // Pipeline Behavior
   128	            input.boundedness(),                    // Boundedness
   129	        )
   130	    }
   131	}
   132	
   133	impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
   134	    fn fmt_as(
   135	        &self,
   136	        t: DisplayFormatType,
   137	        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
   138	    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
   139	        match t {
   140	            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
   141	                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec")
   142	            }
   143	            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
   144	                // TODO: collect info
   145	                write!(f, "")
   146	            }
   147	        }
   148	    }
   149	}
   150	
   151	impl ExecutionPlan for OutputRequirementExec {
   152	    fn name(&self) -> &'static str {
   153	        "OutputRequirementExec"
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    fn as_any(&self) -> &dyn std::any::Any {
   157	        self
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    fn properties(&self) -> &PlanProperties {
   161	        &self.cache
   162	    }
   163	
   164	    fn benefits_from_input_partitioning(&self) -> Vec<bool> {
   165	        vec![false]
   166	    }
   167	
   168	    fn required_input_distribution(&self) -> Vec<Distribution> {
   169	        vec![self.dist_requirement.clone()]
   170	    }
   171	
   172	    fn maintains_input_order(&self) -> Vec<bool> {
   173	        vec![true]
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    fn children(&self) -> Vec<&Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   177	        vec![&self.input]
   178	    }
   179	
   180	    fn required_input_ordering(&self) -> Vec<Option<OrderingRequirements>> {
   181	        vec![self.order_requirement.clone()]
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    fn with_new_children(
   185	        self: Arc<Self>,
   186	        mut children: Vec<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>,
   187	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   188	        Ok(Arc::new(Self::new(
   189	            children.remove(0), // has a single child
   190	            self.order_requirement.clone(),
   191	            self.dist_requirement.clone(),
   192	        )))
   193	    }
   194	
   195	    fn execute(
   196	        &self,
   197	        _partition: usize,
   198	        _context: Arc<TaskContext>,
   199	    ) -> Result<SendableRecordBatchStream> {
   200	        unreachable!();
   201	    }
   202	
   203	    fn statistics(&self) -> Result<Statistics> {
   204	        self.input.partition_statistics(None)
   205	    }
   206	
   207	    fn partition_statistics(&self, partition: Option<usize>) -> Result<Statistics> {
   208	        self.input.partition_statistics(partition)
   209	    }
   210	
   211	    fn try_swapping_with_projection(
   212	        &self,
   213	        projection: &ProjectionExec,
   214	    ) -> Result<Option<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>>> {
   215	        // If the projection does not narrow the schema, we should not try to push it down:
   216	        let proj_exprs = projection.expr();
   217	        if proj_exprs.len() >= projection.input().schema().fields().len() {
   218	            return Ok(None);
   219	        }
   220	
   221	        let mut requirements = self.required_input_ordering().swap_remove(0);
   222	        if let Some(reqs) = requirements {
   223	            let mut updated_reqs = vec![];
   224	            let (lexes, soft) = reqs.into_alternatives();
   225	            for lex in lexes.into_iter() {
   226	                let Some(updated_lex) = update_ordering_requirement(lex, proj_exprs)?
   227	                else {
   228	                    return Ok(None);
   229	                };
   230	                updated_reqs.push(updated_lex);
   231	            }
   232	            requirements = OrderingRequirements::new_alternatives(updated_reqs, soft);
   233	        }
   234	
   235	        let dist_req = match &self.required_input_distribution()[0] {
   236	            Distribution::HashPartitioned(exprs) => {
   237	                let mut updated_exprs = vec![];
   238	                for expr in exprs {
   239	                    let Some(new_expr) = update_expr(expr, projection.expr(), false)?
   240	                    else {
   241	                        return Ok(None);
   242	                    };
   243	                    updated_exprs.push(new_expr);
   244	                }
   245	                Distribution::HashPartitioned(updated_exprs)
   246	            }
   247	            dist => dist.clone(),
   248	        };
   249	
   250	        make_with_child(projection, &self.input()).map(|input| {
   251	            let e = OutputRequirementExec::new(input, requirements, dist_req);
   252	            Some(Arc::new(e) as _)
   253	        })
   254	    }
   255	}
   256	
   257	impl PhysicalOptimizerRule for OutputRequirements {
   258	    fn optimize(
   259	        &self,
   260	        plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   261	        _config: &ConfigOptions,
   262	    ) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   263	        match self.mode {
   264	            RuleMode::Add => require_top_ordering(plan),
   265	            RuleMode::Remove => plan
   266	                .transform_up(|plan| {
   267	                    if let Some(sort_req) =
   268	                        plan.as_any().downcast_ref::<OutputRequirementExec>()
   269	                    {
   270	                        Ok(Transformed::yes(sort_req.input()))
   271	                    } else {
   272	                        Ok(Transformed::no(plan))
   273	                    }
   274	                })
   275	                .data(),
   276	        }
   277	    }
   278	
   279	    fn name(&self) -> &str {
   280	        "OutputRequirements"
   281	    }
   282	
   283	    fn schema_check(&self) -> bool {
   284	        true
   285	    }
   286	}
   287	
   288	/// This functions adds ancillary `OutputRequirementExec` to the physical plan, so that
   289	/// global requirements are not lost during optimization.
   290	fn require_top_ordering(plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>) -> Result<Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>> {
   291	    let (new_plan, is_changed) = require_top_ordering_helper(plan)?;
   292	    if is_changed {
   293	        Ok(new_plan)
   294	    } else {
   295	        // Add `OutputRequirementExec` to the top, with no specified ordering and distribution requirement.
   296	        Ok(Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
   297	            new_plan,
   298	            // there is no ordering requirement
   299	            None,
   300	            Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution,
   301	        )) as _)
   302	    }
   303	}
   304	
   305	/// Helper function that adds an ancillary `OutputRequirementExec` to the given plan.
   306	/// First entry in the tuple is resulting plan, second entry indicates whether any
   307	/// `OutputRequirementExec` is added to the plan.
   308	fn require_top_ordering_helper(
   309	    plan: Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>,
   310	) -> Result<(Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>, bool)> {
   311	    let mut children = plan.children();
   312	    // Global ordering defines desired ordering in the final result.
   313	    if children.len() != 1 {
   314	        Ok((plan, false))
   315	    } else if let Some(sort_exec) = plan.as_any().downcast_ref::<SortExec>() {
   316	        // In case of constant columns, output ordering of the `SortExec` would
   317	        // be an empty set. Therefore; we check the sort expression field to
   318	        // assign the requirements.
   319	        let req_ordering = sort_exec.expr();
   320	        let req_dist = sort_exec.required_input_distribution().swap_remove(0);
   321	        let reqs = OrderingRequirements::from(req_ordering.clone());
   322	        Ok((
   323	            Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(plan, Some(reqs), req_dist)) as _,
   324	            true,
   325	        ))
   326	    } else if let Some(spm) = plan.as_any().downcast_ref::<SortPreservingMergeExec>() {
   327	        let reqs = OrderingRequirements::from(spm.expr().clone());
   328	        Ok((
   329	            Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
   330	                plan,
   331	                Some(reqs),
   332	                Distribution::SinglePartition,
   333	            )) as _,
   334	            true,
   335	        ))
   336	    } else if plan.maintains_input_order()[0]
   337	        && (plan.required_input_ordering()[0]
   338	            .as_ref()
   339	            .is_none_or(|o| matches!(o, OrderingRequirements::Soft(_))))
   340	    {
   341	        // Keep searching for a `SortExec` as long as ordering is maintained,
   342	        // and on-the-way operators do not themselves require an ordering.
   343	        // When an operator requires an ordering, any `SortExec` below can not
   344	        // be responsible for (i.e. the originator of) the global ordering.
   345	        let (new_child, is_changed) =
   346	            require_top_ordering_helper(Arc::clone(children.swap_remove(0)))?;
   347	        Ok((plan.with_new_children(vec![new_child])?, is_changed))
   348	    } else {
   349	        // Stop searching, there is no global ordering desired for the query.
   350	        Ok((plan, false))
   351	    }
   352	}
   353

   355

    fn fmt_as(&self, t: DisplayFormatType, f: &mut Formatter) -> fmt::Result {

pub enum Distribution {
    /// Unspecified distribution
    UnspecifiedDistribution,
    /// A single partition is required
    SinglePartition,
    /// Requires children to be distributed in such a way that the same
    /// values of the keys end up in the same partition
    HashPartitioned(Vec<Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>>),
}

impl Distribution {
    /// Creates a `Partitioning` that satisfies this `Distribution`
    pub fn create_partitioning(self, partition_count: usize) -> Partitioning {
        match self {
            Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution => {
                Partitioning::UnknownPartitioning(partition_count)
            }
            Distribution::SinglePartition => Partitioning::UnknownPartitioning(1),
            Distribution::HashPartitioned(expr) => {
                Partitioning::Hash(expr, partition_count)
            }
        }
    }
}

impl Display for Distribution {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter) -> fmt::Result {
        match self {
            Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution => write!(f, "Unspecified"),
            Distribution::SinglePartition => write!(f, "SinglePartition"),
            Distribution::HashPartitioned(exprs) => {

impl Display for Distribution {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter) -> fmt::Result {
        match self {
            Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution => write!(f, "Unspecified"),
            Distribution::SinglePartition => write!(f, "SinglePartition"),
            Distribution::HashPartitioned(exprs) => {
                write!(f, "HashPartitioned[{}])", format_physical_expr_list(exprs))
            }
        }
    }
}

/// alternatives can be either hard or soft, depending on whether the operator
/// can work without an input ordering.
///
/// # Invariants
///
/// The following always hold true for a `OrderingRequirements`:
///
/// 1. It is non-degenerate, meaning it contains at least one ordering. The
///    absence of an input ordering requirement is represented by a `None` value
///    in `ExecutionPlan` APIs, which return an `Option<OrderingRequirements>`.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq)]
pub enum OrderingRequirements {
    /// The operator is not able to work without one of these requirements.
    Hard(Vec<LexRequirement>),
    /// The operator can benefit from these input orderings when available,
    /// but can still work in the absence of any input ordering.
    Soft(Vec<LexRequirement>),
}

impl OrderingRequirements {
    /// Creates a new instance from the given alternatives. If an empty list of
    /// alternatives are given, returns `None`.
    pub fn new_alternatives(
        alternatives: impl IntoIterator<Item = LexRequirement>,
        soft: bool,
    ) -> Option<Self> {
        let alternatives = alternatives.into_iter().collect::<Vec<_>>();
        (!alternatives.is_empty()).then(|| {
            if soft {
                Self::Soft(alternatives)
            } else {
                Self::Hard(alternatives)
            }
        })
    }

    /// Creates a new instance with a single hard requirement.
    pub fn new(requirement: LexRequirement) -> Self {
        Self::Hard(vec![requirement])
    }

    /// Creates a new instance with a single soft requirement.
    pub fn new_soft(requirement: LexRequirement) -> Self {
        Self::Soft(vec![requirement])
    }

    /// Adds an alternative requirement to the list of alternatives.
    pub fn add_alternative(&mut self, requirement: LexRequirement) {
        match self {
            Self::Hard(alts) | Self::Soft(alts) => alts.push(requirement),
        }
    }

    /// Returns the first (i.e. most preferred) `LexRequirement` among
    /// alternative requirements.
    pub fn into_single(self) -> LexRequirement {
        match self {
            Self::Hard(mut alts) | Self::Soft(mut alts) => alts.swap_remove(0),
        }
    }

    /// Returns a reference to the first (i.e. most preferred) `LexRequirement`
    /// among alternative requirements.
    pub fn first(&self) -> &LexRequirement {
        match self {
            Self::Hard(alts) | Self::Soft(alts) => &alts[0],
        }
    }

    /// Returns all alternatives as a vector of `LexRequirement` objects and a
--
            Self::Soft(alts) => (alts, true),
        }
    }
}

impl From<LexRequirement> for OrderingRequirements {
    fn from(requirement: LexRequirement) -> Self {
        Self::new(requirement)
    }
}

impl From<LexOrdering> for OrderingRequirements {
    fn from(ordering: LexOrdering) -> Self {
        Self::new(ordering.into())
    }
}

impl Deref for OrderingRequirements {
    type Target = [LexRequirement];

    fn deref(&self) -> &Self::Target {
        match &self {
            Self::Hard(alts) | Self::Soft(alts) => alts.as_slice(),
        }
    }
}

    fn deref_mut(&mut self) -> &mut Self::Target {

/// order, then by column `b` in *any* (ascending or descending) order. The
/// ordering is non-degenerate, meaning it contains at least one element, and
/// it is duplicate-free, meaning it does not contain multiple entries for the
/// same column.
///
/// Note that a `LexRequirement` need not enforce the uniqueness of its sort
/// expressions after construction like a `LexOrdering` does, because it provides
/// no mutation methods. If such methods become necessary, we will need to
/// enforce uniqueness like the latter object.
#[derive(Debug, Clone, PartialEq)]
pub struct LexRequirement {
    reqs: Vec<PhysicalSortRequirement>,
}

impl LexRequirement {
    /// Creates a new [`LexRequirement`] from the given vector of sort expressions.
    /// If the vector is empty, returns `None`.
    pub fn new(reqs: impl IntoIterator<Item = PhysicalSortRequirement>) -> Option<Self> {
        let (non_empty, requirements) = Self::construct(reqs);
        non_empty.then_some(requirements)
    }

    /// Returns the leading `PhysicalSortRequirement` of the `LexRequirement`.
    /// Note that this function does not return an `Option`, as a `LexRequirement`
    /// is always non-degenerate (i.e. it contains at least one element).
    pub fn first(&self) -> &PhysicalSortRequirement {
        // Can safely `unwrap` because `LexRequirement` is non-degenerate:
        self.reqs.first().unwrap()
    }

    /// Constructs a new `LexRequirement` from the given sort requirements w/o
    /// enforcing non-degeneracy. This function is used internally and is not
    /// meant (or safe) for external use.
    fn construct(
        reqs: impl IntoIterator<Item = PhysicalSortRequirement>,
    ) -> (bool, Self) {
        let mut set = HashSet::new();
        let reqs = reqs
            .into_iter()
            .filter_map(|r| set.insert(Arc::clone(&r.expr)).then_some(r))
            .collect();
        (!set.is_empty(), Self { reqs })
    }
}

impl<const N: usize> From<[PhysicalSortRequirement; N]> for LexRequirement {
    fn from(value: [PhysicalSortRequirement; N]) -> Self {

        //       when Rust supports it.
        assert!(N > 0);

/// Without sort options (`A`, None):
/// * `ORDER BY A DESC NULLS FIRST` matches
/// * `ORDER BY A ASC  NULLS FIRST` matches (`ASC` and `NULL` options ignored)
/// * `ORDER BY B DESC NULLS FIRST` does not match  (different expr)
#[derive(Clone, Debug)]
pub struct PhysicalSortRequirement {
    /// Physical expression representing the column to sort
    pub expr: Arc<dyn PhysicalExpr>,
    /// Option to specify how the given column should be sorted.
    /// If unspecified, there are no constraints on sort options.
    pub options: Option<SortOptions>,
}

impl PartialEq for PhysicalSortRequirement {
    fn eq(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {
        self.options == other.options && self.expr.eq(&other.expr)
    }
}

impl Display for PhysicalSortRequirement {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter) -> fmt::Result {
        let opts_string = self.options.as_ref().map_or("NA", to_str);
        write!(f, "{} {}", self.expr, opts_string)
    }
}

pub fn format_physical_sort_requirement_list(
    exprs: &[PhysicalSortRequirement],
) -> impl Display + '_ {
    struct DisplayWrapper<'a>(&'a [PhysicalSortRequirement]);
    impl Display for DisplayWrapper<'_> {
        fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_>) -> fmt::Result {
            let mut iter = self.0.iter();
            write!(f, "[")?;
            if let Some(expr) = iter.next() {
                write!(f, "{expr}")?;
            }
            for expr in iter {
                write!(f, ", {expr}")?;
            }
            write!(f, "]")?;
            Ok(())
        }
    }
    DisplayWrapper(exprs)
}

use datafusion::prelude::*;

use datafusion_physical_optimizer::output_requirements::OutputRequirementExec;
use datafusion_physical_plan::ExecutionPlan;
use datafusion_physical_plan::placeholder_row::PlaceholderRowExec;
use datafusion_physical_plan::displayable;
use datafusion_expr::col;

#[tokio::main]
async fn main() -> Result<()> {
    // Create a simple plan to test
    let schema = Arc::new(datafusion::arrow::datatypes::Schema::new(vec![
        datafusion::arrow::datatypes::Field::new("a", datafusion::arrow::datatypes::DataType::Int32, false),
        datafusion::arrow::datatypes::Field::new("b", datafusion::arrow::datatypes::DataType::Int32, false),
    ]));
    
    let placeholder = PlaceholderRowExec::new(schema.clone());
    
    // Create a sort requirement
    let sort_req = PhysicalSortRequirement::new(
        Arc::new(datafusion_physical_expr::expressions::Column::new("a", 0)),
        Some(datafusion_expr::SortOptions::default()),
    );
    let ordering_reqs = OrderingRequirements::new([sort_req].into());
    
    // Create OutputRequirementExec with different distributions
    println!("=== Test 1: UnspecifiedDistribution with no ordering ===");
    let plan1 = Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
        Arc::new(placeholder.clone()),
        None,
        Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution,
    )) as Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>;
    println!("{}", displayable(plan1.as_ref()).indent(true));
    
    println!("\n=== Test 2: SinglePartition with ordering ===");
    let plan2 = Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
        Arc::new(placeholder.clone()),
        ordering_reqs.clone(),
        Distribution::SinglePartition,
    )) as Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>;
    println!("{}", displayable(plan2.as_ref()).indent(true));
    
    println!("\n=== Test 3: HashPartitioned with ordering ===");
    let hash_exprs = vec![
        Arc::new(datafusion_physical_expr::expressions::Column::new("a", 0)) as Arc<dyn datafusion_physical_expr_common::physical_expr::PhysicalExpr>,
        Arc::new(datafusion_physical_expr::expressions::Column::new("b", 1)) as Arc<dyn datafusion_physical_expr_common::physical_expr::PhysicalExpr>,
    ];
    let plan3 = Arc::new(OutputRequirementExec::new(
        Arc::new(placeholder),
        ordering_reqs,
        Distribution::HashPartitioned(hash_exprs),
    )) as Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>;
    println!("{}", displayable(plan3.as_ref()).indent(true));
    
    Ok(())
}

    67	/// Create a sorted Csv exec
    68	fn csv_exec_sorted(
    69	    schema: &SchemaRef,
    70	    sort_exprs: impl IntoIterator<Item = PhysicalSortExpr>,
    71	) -> Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan> {
    72	    let mut builder = FileScanConfigBuilder::new(
    73	        ObjectStoreUrl::parse("test:///").unwrap(),
    74	        schema.clone(),
    75	        Arc::new(CsvSource::new(false, 0, 0)),
    76	    )
    77	    .with_file(PartitionedFile::new("x".to_string(), 100));
    78	    if let Some(ordering) = LexOrdering::new(sort_exprs) {
    79	        builder = builder.with_output_ordering(vec![ordering]);
    80	    }
    81	
    82	    let config = builder.build();
    83	    DataSourceExec::from_data_source(config)
    84	}

impl Display for Distribution {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut fmt::Formatter) -> fmt::Result {
        match self {
            Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution => write!(f, "Unspecified"),
            Distribution::SinglePartition => write!(f, "SinglePartition"),
            Distribution::HashPartitioned(exprs) => {
                write!(f, "HashPartitioned[{}])", format_physical_expr_list(exprs))
            }
        }
    }
}

impl Deref for LexRequirement {
    type Target = [PhysicalSortRequirement];

    fn deref(&self) -> &Self::Target {
        self.reqs.as_slice()
    }
}

impl IntoIterator for LexRequirement {
    type Item = PhysicalSortRequirement;
    type IntoIter = IntoIter<Self::Item>;

    fn into_iter(self) -> Self::IntoIter {
        self.reqs.into_iter()
    }
}

impl Display for PhysicalSortRequirement {
    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter) -> fmt::Result {
        let opts_string = self.options.as_ref().map_or("NA", to_str);
        write!(f, "{} {}", self.expr, opts_string)
    }
}

OBSERVATION:

fn to_str(options: &SortOptions) -> &str {
    match (options.descending, options.nulls_first) {
        (true, true) => "DESC",
        (true, false) => "DESC NULLS LAST",
        (false, true) => "ASC",
        (false, false) => "ASC NULLS LAST",
    }
}

// Cross-conversion utilities between `PhysicalSortExpr` and `PhysicalSortRequirement`
impl From<PhysicalSortExpr> for PhysicalSortRequirement {
    fn from(value: PhysicalSortExpr) -> Self {
        Self::new(value.expr, Some(value.options))
    }
}

impl From<PhysicalSortRequirement> for PhysicalSortExpr {
    /// The default sort options `ASC, NULLS LAST` when the requirement does
    /// not specify sort options. This default is consistent with PostgreSQL.
    ///
    /// Reference: <https://www.postgresql.org/docs/current/queries-order.html>

impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
    fn fmt_as(
        &self,
        t: DisplayFormatType,
        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
        match t {
            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec:")?;
                
                // Display order requirement if present
                if let Some(ref reqs) = self.order_requirement {
                    use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::format_physical_sort_requirement_list;
                    write!(f, " order_requirement=[{}],", format_physical_sort_requirement_list(reqs.first()))?;
                }
                
                // Display distribution requirement
                write!(f, " dist_requirement={}", self.dist_requirement)?;
                
                Ok(())
            }
            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
                // TODO: collect info
                write!(f, "")
            }
        }
    }
}

use std::sync::Arc;
use datafusion_physical_optimizer::output_requirements::OutputRequirementExec;
use datafusion_physical_plan::{DisplayAs, DisplayFormatType, ExecutionPlan};
use datafusion_physical_plan::placeholder_row::PlaceholderRowExec;
use datafusion_physical_expr::Distribution;
use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::{OrderingRequirements, PhysicalSortRequirement};
use datafusion_physical_expr::expressions::Column;
use arrow::compute::SortOptions;
use arrow::datatypes::{DataType, Field, Schema};

fn main() {
    println!("Testing OutputRequirementExec display...\n");

    // Create a simple schema
    let schema = Arc::new(Schema::new(vec![
        Field::new("a", DataType::Int32, false),
        Field::new("b", DataType::Int32, false),
    ]));

    // Create a placeholder input plan
    let input = Arc::new(PlaceholderRowExec::new(schema.clone())) as Arc<dyn ExecutionPlan>;

    // Test 1: No order requirement, Unspecified distribution
    println!("Test 1: No order requirement, Unspecified distribution");
    let exec1 = OutputRequirementExec::new(
        input.clone(),
        None,
        Distribution::UnspecifiedDistribution,
    );
    let mut output = String::new();
    exec1.fmt_as(DisplayFormatType::Default, &mut std::fmt::Formatter::new(&mut output)).unwrap();
    println!("Output: {}\n", output);

    // Test 2: With order requirement, SinglePartition distribution
    println!("Test 2: With order requirement (a ASC), SinglePartition distribution");
    let sort_req = PhysicalSortRequirement::new(
        Arc::new(Column::new("a", 0)),
        Some(SortOptions::default()),
    );
    let ordering_reqs = OrderingRequirements::new([sort_req].into());
    let exec2 = OutputRequirementExec::new(
        input.clone(),
        ordering_reqs,
        Distribution::SinglePartition,
    );
    let display_str = format!("{}", exec2);
    println!("Output: {}\n", display_str);

    // Test 3: With order requirement (multiple columns), HashPartitioned distribution
    println!("Test 3: With order requirement (a ASC, b DESC), HashPartitioned distribution");
    let sort_req1 = PhysicalSortRequirement::new(
        Arc::new(Column::new("a", 0)),
        Some(SortOptions {
            descending: false,
            nulls_first: false,
        }),
    );
    let sort_req2 = PhysicalSortRequirement::new(
        Arc::new(Column::new("b", 1)),
        Some(SortOptions {
            descending: true,
            nulls_first: true,
        }),
    );
    let ordering_reqs = OrderingRequirements::new([sort_req1, sort_req2].into());
    let hash_exprs = vec![
        Arc::new(Column::new("a", 0)) as Arc<dyn datafusion_physical_expr_common::physical_expr::PhysicalExpr>,
    ];
    let exec3 = OutputRequirementExec::new(
        input.clone(),
        ordering_reqs,
        Distribution::HashPartitioned(hash_exprs),
    );
    let display_str = format!("{}", exec3);
    println!("Output: {}\n", display_str);

    println!("All tests completed successfully!");
}
'

Looking at my implementation again:

```rust
impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
    fn fmt_as(
        &self,
        t: DisplayFormatType,
        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
        match t {
            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec:")?;
                
                // Display order requirement if present
                if let Some(ref reqs) = self.order_requirement {
                    use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::format_physical_sort_requirement_list;
                    write!(f, " order_requirement=[{}],", format_physical_sort_requirement_list(reqs.first()))?;
                }
                
                // Display distribution requirement
                write!(f, " dist_requirement={}", self.dist_requirement)?;
                
                Ok(())
            }
            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
                // TODO: collect info
                write!(f, "")
            }
        }
    }
}
```

This implementation:
1. ✓ Always displays "OutputRequirementExec:"
2. ✓ If there's an order_requirement, displays it in format `order_requirement=[...]`
3. ✓ Always displays the dist_requirement in format `dist_requirement=...`

The output format would be:
- With order requirement: `OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col@0 ASC], dist_requirement=SinglePartition`
- Without order requirement: `OutputRequirementExec: dist_requirement=Unspecified`

This matches the requirements from the PR description: "It'll be helpful to include `order_requirement` and `dist_requirement`".

Now let me think about edge cases:

1. **No order requirement**: Handled - we only print order_requirement if it's Some()
2. **Multiple sort expressions in order requirement**: Handled - format_physical_sort_requirement_list handles this
3. **Different distribution types**: Handled - Distribution already has a Display implementation
4. **TreeRender format**: Left empty as before (TODO remains)

str_replace_editor create /testbed/IMPLEMENTATION_SUMMARY.md --file_text '# OutputRequirementExec Display Enhancement

## Summary of Changes

Modified the `DisplayAs` implementation for `OutputRequirementExec` in 
`/testbed/repo/datafusion/physical-optimizer/src/output_requirements.rs` to include
more information when displaying the execution plan.

## What Changed

### Before
```
OutputRequirementExec
```

### After
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col@0 ASC], dist_requirement=SinglePartition
```

## Implementation Details

The `fmt_as` method now:

1. Always displays the base name: `OutputRequirementExec:`
2. Conditionally displays the order requirement if present:
   - Format: `order_requirement=[expr1 ASC, expr2 DESC, ...]`
   - Uses the existing `format_physical_sort_requirement_list` function
   - Displays the first alternative from OrderingRequirements
3. Always displays the distribution requirement:
   - Format: `dist_requirement=<Distribution>`
   - Uses the existing `Display` impl for `Distribution`
   - Examples: `SinglePartition`, `Unspecified`, `HashPartitioned[col1, col2])`

## Code Changes

File: `datafusion/physical-optimizer/src/output_requirements.rs`
Lines: 133-160

Changed from:
```rust
impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
    fn fmt_as(
        &self,
        t: DisplayFormatType,
        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
        match t {
            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec")
            }
            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
                // TODO: collect info
                write!(f, "")
            }
        }
    }
}
```

To:
```rust
impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
    fn fmt_as(
        &self,
        t: DisplayFormatType,
        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
        match t {
            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec:")?;
                
                // Display order requirement if present
                if let Some(ref reqs) = self.order_requirement {
                    use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::format_physical_sort_requirement_list;
                    write!(f, " order_requirement=[{}],", format_physical_sort_requirement_list(reqs.first()))?;
                }
                
                // Display distribution requirement
                write!(f, " dist_requirement={}", self.dist_requirement)?;
                
                Ok(())
            }
            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
                // TODO: collect info
                write!(f, "")
            }
        }
    }
}
```

## Testing

The implementation:
- ✓ Compiles successfully
- ✓ Follows the existing display format patterns used in other execution plans (e.g., SortExec)
- ✓ Handles edge cases:
  - No order requirement (order_requirement field is None)
  - Multiple sort expressions in the requirement
  - All distribution types (Unspecified, SinglePartition, HashPartitioned)
- ✓ Uses existing utility functions for formatting

## Example Outputs

### Case 1: No order requirement
```
OutputRequirementExec: dist_requirement=Unspecified
```

### Case 2: Single sort expression, SinglePartition
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col@0 ASC], dist_requirement=SinglePartition
```

### Case 3: Multiple sort expressions, HashPartitioned
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[a@0 ASC NULLS LAST, b@1 DESC], dist_requirement=HashPartitioned[a@0, b@1])
```

### Case 4: Complex expression in sort requirement
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[a@0 + b@1 ASC NULLS LAST], dist_requirement=SinglePartition
```

EDGE CASE ANALYSIS

Our implementation handles the following edge cases:

1. ✓ No order requirement (None)
   - Only order_requirement is optional, so we check with if let Some
   - Output: 'OutputRequirementExec: dist_requirement=...'

2. ✓ Single sort expression in order requirement
   - format_physical_sort_requirement_list handles this
   - Output: 'OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col@0 ASC], dist_requirement=...'

3. ✓ Multiple sort expressions in order requirement
   - format_physical_sort_requirement_list handles the list
   - Output: 'OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col1 ASC, col2 DESC], dist_requirement=...'

4. ✓ Complex expressions in sort requirement (e.g., a + b)
   - PhysicalExpr Display handles the expression formatting
   - Output: 'OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[a@0 + b@1 ASC], dist_requirement=...'

5. ✓ Different SortOptions (ASC/DESC, NULLS FIRST/LAST)
   - PhysicalSortRequirement Display includes the options
   - Examples: 'ASC', 'DESC', 'ASC NULLS LAST', 'DESC NULLS FIRST'

6. ✓ UnspecifiedDistribution
   - Distribution Display impl handles this
   - Output: 'dist_requirement=Unspecified'

7. ✓ SinglePartition distribution
   - Distribution Display impl handles this
   - Output: 'dist_requirement=SinglePartition'

8. ✓ HashPartitioned distribution with expressions
   - Distribution Display impl handles this
   - Output: 'dist_requirement=HashPartitioned[col1, col2])'
   - Note: There's a typo in Distribution's Display (extra ')'), but that's pre-existing

9. ✓ OrderingRequirements with alternatives (Hard vs Soft)
   - We display the first (most preferred) alternative using .first()
   - Both Hard and Soft requirements are handled the same for display

10. ✓ DisplayFormatType variants
    - Default and Verbose: Show full information
    - TreeRender: Empty string (TODO remains as before)

======================================
ANALYSIS COMPLETE ✓
======================================

- Conditional display (if let Some) for optional fields
- Delegating to existing Display implementations

str_replace_editor create /testbed/SOLUTION_SUMMARY.md --file_text '# Solution Summary: Enhanced OutputRequirementExec Display

## Problem Statement
The PR requested that the display of `OutputRequirementExec` should include more information, specifically `order_requirement` and `dist_requirement`, to make the physical plan output more informative.

**Before:**
```
05)--------OutputRequirementExec
```

**After:**
```
05)--------OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col@0 ASC], dist_requirement=SinglePartition
```

## Solution

### Modified File
- `datafusion/physical-optimizer/src/output_requirements.rs`

### Changes Made
Updated the `DisplayAs` implementation for `OutputRequirementExec` (lines 133-160) to:

1. **Always display the base name with colon**: `OutputRequirementExec:`
2. **Conditionally display order requirement**: If `order_requirement` is `Some`, display it as `order_requirement=[expr1 opt1, expr2 opt2, ...]`
3. **Always display distribution requirement**: Display as `dist_requirement=<Distribution>`

### Implementation Details

```rust
impl DisplayAs for OutputRequirementExec {
    fn fmt_as(
        &self,
        t: DisplayFormatType,
        f: &mut std::fmt::Formatter,
    ) -> std::fmt::Result {
        match t {
            DisplayFormatType::Default | DisplayFormatType::Verbose => {
                write!(f, "OutputRequirementExec:")?;
                
                // Display order requirement if present
                if let Some(ref reqs) = self.order_requirement {
                    use datafusion_physical_expr_common::sort_expr::format_physical_sort_requirement_list;
                    write!(f, " order_requirement=[{}],", format_physical_sort_requirement_list(reqs.first()))?;
                }
                
                // Display distribution requirement
                write!(f, " dist_requirement={}", self.dist_requirement)?;
                
                Ok(())
            }
            DisplayFormatType::TreeRender => {
                // TODO: collect info
                write!(f, "")
            }
        }
    }
}
```

## Key Design Decisions

1. **Use existing formatting utilities**: Leveraged `format_physical_sort_requirement_list` for consistency with other execution plans
2. **Display first alternative**: For `OrderingRequirements` with multiple alternatives, show the first (most preferred) one
3. **Consistent format**: Follows the pattern used by other execution plans (e.g., `SortExec: expr=[...], preserve_partitioning=[...]`)
4. **Proper handling of optional fields**: Only display `order_requirement` when it exists

## Edge Cases Handled

✓ No order requirement (None)  
✓ Single sort expression  
✓ Multiple sort expressions  
✓ Complex expressions (e.g., `a + b`)  
✓ Different sort options (ASC/DESC, NULLS FIRST/LAST)  
✓ All distribution types (Unspecified, SinglePartition, HashPartitioned)  
✓ OrderingRequirements alternatives (Hard vs Soft)  
✓ All DisplayFormatType variants  

## Example Outputs

### 1. No order requirement, Unspecified distribution
```
OutputRequirementExec: dist_requirement=Unspecified
```

### 2. Single column ASC, SinglePartition
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[col@0 ASC], dist_requirement=SinglePartition
```

### 3. Multiple columns with different options, HashPartitioned
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[a@0 ASC NULLS LAST, b@1 DESC], dist_requirement=HashPartitioned[a@0, b@1])
```

### 4. Complex expression
```
OutputRequirementExec: order_requirement=[a@0 + b@1 ASC NULLS LAST], dist_requirement=SinglePartition
```

## Verification

✓ Code compiles successfully  
✓ No new dependencies added  
✓ Follows existing code patterns  
✓ Minimal, focused changes  
✓ Comprehensive edge case coverage  

## Impact

This change makes the physical plan output more informative and easier to debug by showing:
- What ordering is required at this point in the plan
- What distribution is required at this point in the plan

This is particularly helpful when debugging optimization rules and understanding why certain operators are inserted into the plan.
